      <p>It should be noted that there is a certain amount of variation
        among Cherokee speakers regarding the order of the non-final
        suffixes. We will not attempt to discuss this variation; the
        reader should bear in mind that the preceding chart reflects the
        speech of some Cherokee speakers, while other speakers may use
        verb forms with suffixes occurring in a somewhat different
        order. In particular, for some speakers -ilo- follows the
        suffixes shown at positions 4--6 in the chart, and -ohn- follows
        the suffixes shown at 6--7. A discussion of the individual
        non-final suffixes follows.</p>
      <p><u>-gi-, reversive</u></p>
      <p>form: -gi- before consonants, -gis- before vowels, before -g-,
        and before the instrumental-causative and accidental suffixes;
        (cf. 1-5).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(1) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᏍᎦ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gv¹sga.</td>
            <td>"I'm weaving it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᎩᎠ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gv²gi³ʔa.</td>
            <td>"I'm unweaving it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(2) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᏎᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gv²sẹ³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's weaving it for him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᎩᎡᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gv²gi³ʔe²ha.</td>
            <td>"He's unweaving it for him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(3) <br>
            </td>
            <td colspan="1"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᎩᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">gv²gi³sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was unweaving it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(4) <br>
            </td>
            <td colspan="1"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᎩᏍᏗᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">gv²gi³sdị²ha.</td>
            <td>"he's using it to unweave it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(5) <br>
            </td>
            <td colspan="1"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᎩᏍᏙᏗᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">gv²gi³sdoh²dị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's accidentally unweaving it."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -gi- is used with a number of verbs in Cherokee to
        reverse the basic meaning.</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 283</p>
      <p>comments: -gi- is attached to the final vowel of the verb stem.
        Note that a sequence of -gi- plus -g-, progressive, plus -a,
        present, yields -giʔa, as in (1b). A sequence of -gi- plus -el-,
        dative, yields -giʔel-, as in (6).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(6) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎬᎩᎢᎵ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gv²³gị³ʔe²li. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will unweave it for him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-e-, reversive</u></p>
      <p>form: -e-.</p>
      <p>function: A reverse meaning is achieved in some verbs by
        changing the final stem vowel to -e-, as in (7).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(7) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎿᏬᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹hnạ²wo³sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was dressing."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎿᏪᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹hnạ²we³sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was undressing."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-y-, reversive</u></p>
      <p> form: -y-.</p>
      <p>function: A reverse meaning is achieved for some verbs by
        inserting -y- before the last stem vowel, as in (8).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(8) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏠᎯᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da³dlo²hị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He is putting on his belt."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏠᏱᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da³dlo²hyị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is taking off his belt."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-is-, duplicative</u></p>
      <p>form: -is- before vowels, except as noted below, and -isis-
        before -g-; cf. (9-10).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(9)</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎵᎠ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³si³lọ²ʔa.</td>
            <td>"He is making the same speech repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(10) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᎣᏂᏏᏏᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³si³sgv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was making the same speech."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note, however, that -is- plus -g- plus -a yields the sequence
        -isiha, as in (11).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(11) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᎣᏂᏏᏏᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³sị³ha. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is making the same speech."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>-is becomes -isahn- before the past tense suffix -vʔi and
        before the future imperative -vʔi; cf. (12-13).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(12) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏌᏅᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³sạ³hnv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He made the same speech."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(13)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᏌᏅᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo³ni²si²³sạ³hnvʔi.</td>
            <td>"Make the same speech later."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When followed by the infinitive suffix -di, -is- changes to
        -isoh-, as in (14).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(14) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³hị³sdi u¹du²li.</td>
            <td>"He wants him to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏐᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³si³soh²di u¹du²li.</td>
            <td>"He wants him to make the same speech again."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -is- is used to indicate that the action of the verb
        is being repeated in the same manner as on a previous occasion.
        In (10b), for example, it is understood that the same contents
        used in a previous speech were being repeated.</p>
      <p><u>-is- "become" </u></p>
      <p>form: -isahn- before vowels, see (15), except as noted, and
        -isis- before -g-; see (16).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(15) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏲᏏᏌᏁᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹yo³si²sạ²hne³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He reportedly got hungry."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td colspan="4">
              <hr color="darkgray">
              <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 284</p>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(16)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏲᏏᏏᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹yo³si²si²³sgv³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was getting hungry."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The sequence of -is- plus -g- plus -a yields -isiha, as in
        (17).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(17) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏲᏏᏏᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹yo³si²sị³ha. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is getting hungry."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Rather than -isahn-, -is- is used before the repetitive suffix
        -ilo-; note (18).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(18) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏲᏏᏏᎶᏍᎪᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹yo³si²si²³lo³²sgo³ʔi. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He repeatedly gets hungry."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The form -isan- is used before the dative-benefactive, as in
        (19).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(19) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏲᏏᏌᏁᎭ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹yo³si²sa³²nẹ²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's getting hungry because of him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note that the dative-benefactive suffix also has a meaning
        which may be translated as "because of." This is a third,
        relatively rare function of the dative-benefactive; for the two
        major functions, see the discussion of -el- below.</p>
      <p>function: This suffix apparently occurs with a limited number
        of intransitive verbs of sensation to indicate that the subject
        of the verb is beginning to experience the sensation in
        question.</p>
      <p><u>-ilo-, repetitive</u></p>
      <p>form: -ilo- before vowels, with a glottal stop inserted, as in
        (20); -ilos- before consonants, as in (21). Exceptions are noted
        below.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(20) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏎᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²se³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He reportedly spoke."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏎᎶᎡᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²se²³lọ³ʔe³i.</td>
            <td>"He reportedly spoke over and over. "</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(21)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏎᎶᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³lo³²sgv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was speaking repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>-ilo- changes to -iloj- before the imperative suffix, -a, as in
        (22); note that the imperative suffix -i changes to -a when
        preceded by another suffix.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(22) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²³hi.</td>
            <td>"Speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᎶᏣ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²si²lo²³ja.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -ilo- is used to indicate that the action or state
        expressed by the verb is being repeated several times.</p>
      <p><u>-dan-, instrumental, causative</u></p>
      <p>form: -dan- before vowels, -dis- before -g; cf. (23-24), except
        as noted.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(23) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏓᏁᎴᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²hị²sda³²ne²le³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He reportedly used it to speak with for him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(24)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²hị²sdị²³sgv³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was using it to speak with."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The sequence of -dis- plus -g- yields -dih- before -a, present
        tense; cf. (25).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(25) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²hị²sdi³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's using it to speak with."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The sequence of -dan- plus -di, the infinitive suffix, yields
        -dohdi, as in (26).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(26) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏙᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³hị³sdoh²di u¹du²li.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to use it to speak with."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Before the imperative suffix -a, -dan- changes to -d-, as in
        (27).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(27) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯᏍᏓ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²hị²sda.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Use it to speak with."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: There are two important functions served by -dan-.
        When used with transitive verbs, its presence indicates that
        some instrument is being employed by the animate subject of the
        verb to assist in carrying out the action of the</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 285</p>
      <p>verb. This function is illustrated by (23-27) above. The second
        function is a causative one: -dan- may be used with inherently
        intransitive verbs to show that the action of the verb is being
        performed by an inanimate object indirectly through the
        causality of an animate agent; cf. (28).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(28) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎵᏍᎦᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>al¹sgi³ʔa.</td>
            <td>"He's dancing."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎵᏍᎩᏍᏗᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>al¹sgi³sdị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's making it dance."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>It is possible for -dan- to have the causative function in the
        case of transitive verbs with animate direct objects, as in
        (29), but this is relatively rare. Furthermore, it is understood
        in (29) that the subject of the verb is actively assisting the
        person who is drinking by holding the drink to his lips.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(29) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏗᏔᏍᏗᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹di²tạ²sdị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's causing him to drink."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The use of the causative with transitive verbs is thus allowed
        only when the subject of the verb is understood to be actively
        assisting the animate direct object to perform the action.</p>
      <p>comments: -dan- is attached to the infinitive stem of verbs
        when it is not preceded by another non-final suffix. The
        infinitive stem of verbs may be found by removing the infinitive
        suffix -di from the infinitive form of verbs found in the
        dictionary. The infinitive form of "to speak" is listed in the
        dictionary as u²wo¹ni²³hị³sdi. When the suffix -di and the
        prefix u- are removed, this leaves the infinitive stem
        -wonihis-, to which -dan- is attached.</p>
      <p><u>-dohdan-, unintentional</u></p>
      <p>form: -dohdan- before vowels, -dohdis- before -g-; exceptions
        correspond to the exceptions noted for -dan-. That is, -dohdan-
        plus -g- plus -a yields -dohdih-, as in (30); -dohdan- plus the
        infinitive suffix -di yields -dohdi, as in (31); -dohdan- plus
        -a, imperative, yields -dohda, as in (32).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(30) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎪᏩᏛᏙᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gowh²tvh²doh³dị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's seeing it accidentally."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(31)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎪᏩᏛᏙᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²gowh²tvh²doh³di u¹du²li.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants him to see it accidentally."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(32)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯᏍᏙᏓ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²hị²sdoh²da.</td>
            <td>"Speak unintentionally."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>It should be noted that forms like (32), while bizarre, are
        understandable and illustrate the form which -dohdan- would take
        when followed by the imperative suffix.</p>
      <p>function: The presence of -dohdan- indicates that the action of
        the verb has been performed unintentionally. The adverbs
        "unintentionally" and "accidentally" can both be used in
        translating forms with -dohdan- into English.</p>
      <p><u>-ohn-, completive</u></p>
      <p>form: -ohn- before vowels, -ohvs- before -g- and before the
        infinitive suffix; cf. (33-35).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(33) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏐᏅᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sọ³hnv³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He finished speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(34)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏐᎯᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sọ³hṿ³sga.</td>
            <td>"He's finishing speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(35)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏐᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³sọ³hṿ²sdi u¹du²li.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to finish speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -ohn- is used to refer to the completion of an
        action. Note (36-38).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(36) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏐᎯᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sọ³hṿ³sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is finishing speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(37)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏐᎿ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sọ³hna.</td>
            <td>"He just finished speaking." (-a marks the recent past
              in this form.)</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td colspan="4">
              <hr color="darkgray">
              <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 286</p>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(38)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏐᏂ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²sọ³hni.</td>
            <td>"He will finish speaking (at a specific point in time)."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-el-, dative-benefactive</u></p>
      <p>form: -el- before vowels, -eh- before the infinitive suffix;
        cf. (39-40).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(39) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si.</td>
            <td>"He will speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᎯᏎᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²hị²se²³li.</td>
            <td>"He will speak for him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(40)</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗ. ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³hị³seh²di u¹du²lị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to speak for him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The sequence of -el- plus -g- plus -a yields -eha; see (41).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(41) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎯᏎᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²hị²sẹ³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is speaking for him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -el- is used to show that an action is being
        undertaken on behalf of someone, as in (40-41). This is the
        benefactive function of -el-. The second major function, the
        dative one, is illustrated by (42).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(42) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏁᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹hnẹ³ha. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is giving it to him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The converse of (42) is also achieved in Cherokee by the use of
        -el- in its dative function; note (43).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(43) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏩᎯᏎᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹hwạ²hị³sẹ³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is buying it from him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>A third function of -el- was discussed in relation to (19)
        above.</p>
      <p>comments: Verb stems ending in -s- before -vʔi and exhibiting
        -s- plus -g- plus -a in the present tense (including those stems
        in which -s- plus -g- plus -a yields -ha) require the infinitive
        form of the stem when the stem is directly followed by -el-; cf.
        (44-47).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(44) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏚᏓᏲᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>du¹da³yọ²sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He surrendered."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(45)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᏓᏲᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹da³yọ²sga.</td>
            <td>"He's surrendering."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(46)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏧᏓᏲᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ju²da²yọ³hị³sdi u¹du²lị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants him to surrender."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(47)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᏓᏲᎯᏎᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹da³yọ²hị²sẹ³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's surrendering for him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-idol- "around"</u></p>
      <p>form: -idol- before vowels, -idol- plus -g- yields -idoh-; cf.
        (48-49).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(48) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He spoke."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏙᎸᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³do³²lv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He went around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(49)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏙᎲᎢ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³do³²hv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was going around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The sequence -idol- plus the infinitive suffix -di yields
        -idoh-, as in (50).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(50) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏓᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³si³da¹sdi u¹du²li.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to go around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Before -a, imperative, and -a, recent past, -idol- becomes id-;
        cf. (51-52).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(51) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᏓ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²si²³da.</td>
            <td>"Go around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(52)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏓ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³da.</td>
            <td>"He just now went around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: The presence of -idol- in a verb form indicates
        movement from place to place on the part of the subject of the
        verb. The use of -idol- does not necessarily imply lack of
        purpose on the part of the speaker, or unplanned random</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 287</p>
      <p>movement; (53) could be said of a politician who is going from
        place to place speaking during his campaign.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(53) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏙᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³do³²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is going around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>-idol- can also be used to refer to essentially random movement
        within a small area; (53) could be used in a situation in which
        a person is pacing while talking.</p>
      <p><u>-e- "at intervals"</u></p>
      <p>form: -vs- before vowels and before -di; -e- before -g-; cf.
        (54-56) .</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(54) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He spoke."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sv³sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He spoke at intervals."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(55)</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³sv³²sdi u¹du²lị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to speak at intervals."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(56)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏎᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²se³gv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking at intervals."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>An exception is the form -es- which appears before the future
        tense suffix -i, as in (57).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(57) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏎᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²ga²wo³²ni²se³si.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will speak at intervals."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>A second exception is the change to -ug- before -a, recent
        past, as in the verb gạ²wo³ni²su³²ga "he just now went to
        speak."</p>
      <p>function : -e- is used to indicate that the action of the verb
        takes place at intervals of time or space. Note the spatial
        example in (58).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(58) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎴᏫᏍᏔᏁᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹le²hwị²stạ²ne³ga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He, it's stopping at intervals."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>A second major function of this suffix is to indicate that the
        subject of the verb is going to a certain place in order to
        perform the action of the verb; note (59).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(59) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏎᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²se³ga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is going (to a certain location) in order to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>All forms with -e- are thus ambiguous. (59) could also mean "He
        is speaking at intervals." Form (54b) could also mean "He went
        in order to speak." Which meaning -e- has in a given instance is
        determined by the context.</p>
      <p><u>-ihl- "come to"</u></p>
      <p>form: -ihl- before vowels, -ihis- before -di, -ihl- plus -g-
        yields -ihih; cf. (60-62). -ihl- becomes -ig- before -a, recent
        past and -a, imperative; cf. (63-64).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(60) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏗᎦᏬᏂᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si.</td>
            <td>"He will speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏟ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si²³hli.</td>
            <td>"He will come to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(61)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³hị³sdi u¹du²lị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He wants to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³si³hị²sdi u¹du²lị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants to come speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(62)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎯᎲᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³hị³hv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was coming to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(63)</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³ga.</td>
            <td>"He just now came to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(64)</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²si²³ga.</td>
            <td>"Come to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 288</p>
      <p>function: -ihl- is used to indicate that the subject of the
        verb is coming to the speaker's location in order to perform the
        action of the verb.</p>
      <p><u>-g-, progressive</u></p>
      <p>form: -g-. When preceded by various suffixes, as noted above,
        -g- frequently becomes -h-; note (65).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(65) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎨᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sge³sdi.</td>
            <td>"He will be speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏩᏙᎮᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³do³²he³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will be going around speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>In (65b), -g- changes to -h- because it is preceded by the
        suffix -idol- (see the discussion of -idol- above). Other
        changes involving -g- when preceded by certain suffixes have
        been noted above in the discussions of the individual suffixes.</p>
      <p>-g- also undergoes changes when preceded directly by verb stems
        of various classes of verbs. Note (66) for example, in which the
        sequence of stem final -s- plus -g- plus -a yields -ha. -g-
        remains unchanged, however, in (67), when followed by the past
        tense suffix.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(66) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²ha.</td>
            <td>"He is speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(67)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>For further details regarding the changes which -g- undergoes
        when preceded directly by verb stems, see the discussion of
        Cherokee verbs in the introduction to the dictionary.</p>
      <p>function: -g- is used with verb forms describing an act or
        state in progress or which is habitual. Progressive verb forms
        are shown in (65-67); note the use of -g- in habitual forms such
        as (68).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(68) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎪᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgo³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He speaks habitually."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Perhaps the term "non-punctual" might be more appropriate than
        "progressive" as label for -g-; it is used with verb forms which
        do not refer to a specific point in time, but is not used with
        those which do. To illustrate this distinction, compare (69) and
        (70).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(69) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He spoke." (at a specific point in time)</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(70) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎨᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sge³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will be speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si.</td>
            <td>"He will speak." (at a specific point in time)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comments: See the discussion of the individual final suffixes
        in Section <a href="#I-D">I-D</a> for further illustration of
        the function of -g-.</p>
      <p><u>A concluding note on the non-final suffixes.</u> See the
        list of verb forms at the end of Section <a href="#I-D">I-D</a>
        for additional examples of the non-final suffixes.</p>
      <p>I-D.<a name="I-D"></a> <u>The final suffixes.</u> The suffixes
        described below may occur at the end of verb forms in Cherokee.
        Two or more final suffixes may occur together, and only those
        suffixes which occur in the final box in the chart at the
        beginning of Section <a href="#I-C">I-C</a> are limited to
        occurrence at the end of verb forms. Discussion of the
        individual final suffixes follows.</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 289</p>
      <p><u>-idi, pre-incipient</u></p>
      <p>form: -idi in final position, -idis- before vowels; cf.
        (71-72).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(71) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si⁴di.</td>
            <td>"He is about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(72)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏪᏂᏏᏗᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³di³²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -idi is used to indicate that the subject of the verb
        is about to perform the action of the verb or is about to
        experience the state expressed by the verb. When used without
        reference to past or future time, and when used in a
        non-habitual sense, -idi occurs in final position, as in (71).
        -idi may be followed by the following suffixes: -vʔi, past;
        -eʔi, reportative; -esdi, future progressive; -oʔi, pluperfect;
        -oʔi, habitual. Examples of the co-occurrence of -idi with each
        of these suffixes follow.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(73) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏗᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³di³²sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(74)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏗᏎᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³di³²se³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was reportedly about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(75)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏗᏎᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³di³²se³sdi.</td>
            <td>"He will be about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(76)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏄᏬᏂᏏᏗᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>nu²³wo³²ni²si²³di³²so⁴ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was already about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(77)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏗᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³di³²so³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He is habitually about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comments: -idi cannot occur with the imperative suffixes. When
        it is used with suffixes which refer to past or future time, as
        in (73-76), the distinction between progressive and punctual
        time is neutralized. (73), for example, can be used in a
        sentence like "He was about to speak when I arrived" or in a
        sentence like "He was about to speak for an instant."</p>
      <p>A variant form of -idi, -idena, is sometimes used. This form
        can only be followed by the question suffixes -sgo and -ju and
        is thus limited to present time. When it is used, as in (78), it
        implies that the action to be performed will occur immediately.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(78) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎦᎿᏂᏕᎾ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²ga²hnạ²ni²de⁴na.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"It's about to rain." (immediately)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>-idi requires the use of the Set B pronoun prefixes.</p>
      <p><u>-i, future</u></p>
      <p>form: -i in final position or when followed by a suffix
        beginning with a consonant; cf. (79-80). -is- when followed by a
        vowel, as in (81).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(79) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si.</td>
            <td>"He's going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(80)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏍᎦᎪ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²sị²sgo?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he going to speak?"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(81)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si³sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>function: -i is ordinarily used to indicate that the subject of
        the verb will perform the action of the verb at a point of time
        in the future. Contrast the punctual future of (79) with the
        future progressive of (82) .</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(82) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎨᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sge³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will be speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>(79) can be used in sentences like "He's going to speak at
        2:00" while (82) is appropriate in sentences such as "He will be
        speaking when I get there."</p>
      <p>-i can also be used with the past tense suffix -vʔi, as in
        (83).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(83) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si³sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 290</p>
      <p>There is no distinction between the punctual and the
        progressive in forms like (83), which imply that the subject of
        the verb was intending to perform the action of the verb at some
        point in the future. Forms like (83) are neutral with respect to
        whether the action was actually performed subsequently or not.</p>
      <p>-i can be followed by the pluperfect -oʔi, as in (84).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(84) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏂᏗᎦᏬᏂᏏᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>nị²dị²gạ²wo³ni²si³so⁴ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was already going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The habitual can be used with -i to indicate that the subject
        of the verb habitually intends to speak, as in (85).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(85) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏗᎦᏬᏂᏏᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dị²gạ²wo³²ni²si³so³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He always intends to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The future progressive -esdi can also follow i-; note (86).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(86) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏗᎦᏬᏂᏏᏎᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dị²gạ²wo³²ni²si³se³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will be going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Form (86) could be used in response to the question "What will
        he be doing at 1:30?" if the person in question is due to speak
        at 2:00. On the other hand, (79) would be the appropriate
        response to the question "What will he do at 2:00?"</p>
      <p>-i can also be followed by -eʔi, the reportative past, as in
        (87).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(87) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏗᎦᏬᏂᏏᏎᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dị²gạ²wo³²ni²si³se³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was reportedly going to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-vʔi, past</u></p>
      <p>form: -vʔi.</p>
      <p>function: This suffix can only be used with verb forms
        referring to past actions or states which were directly
        experienced or witnessed by the speaker. In (88), for example,
        the speaker is understood to have witnessed the act of speaking.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(88) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He spoke."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When -vʔi is used without being preceded by -g-, it is
        understood to refer to a specific point of time in the past. For
        instance, (88) is understood to refer to a single act of
        speaking at some past time. The past progressive is formed by
        the use of -g- followed by -vʔi; note (89).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(89) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎬᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>See also the discussions of -idi and -i above. The future
        imperative is formed by -vʔi, as in (90).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(90) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo³ni²sv²ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak (later)."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comment: The final -ʔi of suffixes consisting of a vowel plus
        -ʔi is optional. When another suffix follows, the final -ʔi may
        or may not be present.</p>
      <p><u>-eʔi, reportative </u></p>
      <p>form: -eʔi.</p>
      <p>function: This suffix functions as does -vʔi, except that it is
        understood that the speaker did not directly experience or
        witness the action or state expressed by the verb. Compare
        (91-92) with (88-89).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(91) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏎᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²se³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He reportedly spoke."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(92)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎨᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sge³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He was reportedly speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 291</p>
      <p><u>-esdi, future progressive</u></p>
      <p>form: -esdi.</p>
      <p>function: -esdi is used to indicate that the action or state
        expressed by the verb will be taking place during a period of
        time in the future; note (93).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(93) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎨᏍᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sge³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He will be speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>See also (86) above for the use of -esdi following the future
        tense suffix -i. -esdi may also be used to form imperatives in
        the future progressive; note (94).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(94) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏍᎨᏍᏗ.&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo³ni²sge³sdi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Be speaking." (as in "Be speaking when I get there.")</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>With some verbs, imperative forms can only be formed by the use
        of -esdi. These verbs can be found by checking the imperative
        entry for each verb in the dictionary.</p>
      <p><u>-oʔi, pluperfect</u></p>
      <p>form: -oʔi.</p>
      <p>function: -oʔi is used with the prefix n- (see Section <a
          href="#I-A">I-A</a>) to indicate that the action or state
        expressed by the verb had already taken place prior to a
        subsequent point in time; note (95).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(95) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏄᏬᏂᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>nu²³wo³²ni²so⁴ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He had already spoken." (prior to some other event)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comment: -oʔi does not occur with the progressive -g-.</p>
      <p><u>-oʔi, habitual</u></p>
      <p>form: -oʔi.</p>
      <p>function: This suffix is used to indicate that the action or
        state expressed by the verb is habitual, as in (96-97).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(96) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏍᎪᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²sgo³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He habitually speaks."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note the uses of -oʔi with -idi and -i; see (77) and (85).</p>
      <p>Forms like (96) may be negated in the usual way, with the
        addition of the negative prefix and the use of hla, as in (97) .</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(97) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: middle;">Ꮭ ᏱᎦᏬᏂᏍᎪᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hla<sup>3 </sup>yị²gạ²wo³²ni²sgo³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He doesn't speak habitually." </td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note also the negative use of -oʔi in forms like (98).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(98) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">Ꮭ ᏳᏬᏂᏐᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hla³ yu²³wo³²ni²so³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He never speaks." (although he could)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-di, infinitive</u></p>
      <p>form: -di.</p>
      <p>function: -di is directly attached to the infinitive stem,
        which is given for each verb in the dictionary. Note that
        infinitives take the Set B subject pronoun prefixes, as in
        (99-100).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(99)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u²wo¹ni²³hị³sdi u¹du²lị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He wants him to speak" or "He wants to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(100) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎩᏬᏂᎯᏍᏗ ᎤᏚᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²gị²wo¹ni²³hị³sdi u¹du²lị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He wants me to speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>For further discussion of the infinitive suffix, see Section <a
          href="#II-E">II-E</a>.</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 292</p>
      <p><u>-a, present</u></p>
      <p>form: -a.</p>
      <p>function: When this suffix directly follows -g-, it indicates
        that the action or state expressed by the verb is in progress at
        present, as in (101).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(101) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᏓᏲᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹da³yọ²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is surrendering."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When -a is not preceded by -g-, it indicates that an action has
        just been completed. This function of -a is usually referred to
        as the recent past. The basic meaning of -a still seems to be
        present time, however; the function of the recent past is to
        indicate that an action has just been completed in the present.</p>
      <p>-a is also used with present imperatives, as in (102).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(102) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᎶᏣ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²si²³lo³ja.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak over and over."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note, however, that -a is used with imperatives only when
        preceded by another suffix. -a changes to -i in imperative forms
        in which no other suffix intervenes, as in (103).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(103) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²³hi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Motion verbs are exceptional with respect to -a. -i is added
        directly to the stem in present tense forms; note (104).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(104) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏍᎯᎵ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹hịʔ³li.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's driving."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When another suffix intervenes, however, -a marks the present
        tense, as in (105).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(105) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎯᎵᏙᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹hịʔ³li²³do³²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's driving around."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The imperative of motion verbs is formed by adding the suffix
        -e- "at intervals" followed by -a, as in (106).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(106) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᎯᎷᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²hịʔ²lu¹ga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Drive."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When the dative-benefactive suffix occurs directly preceding
        the imperative suffix, it drops, and -a changes to -i, as in
        (107).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(107) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hi²wo¹ni²hị²si.</td>
            <td>"Speak for him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Another major function of -a is to show doubt on the part of
        the speaker regarding whether the action of the verb has
        actually been performed, as in (108).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(108) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏳᏬᏂᏌ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yụ³wo³ni²sa.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He may have spoken."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note that the construction used in (108) requires the use of
        the Set B prefixes together with the non-factual prefix y-. In
        addition, -a may not be preceded by -g-, the progressive suffix,
        in past forms expressing doubt. When -a is used with present
        tense forms expressing doubt, -g- precedes it, as in (109); note
        that -g- plus -a yields -ha in the case of "speak."</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(109) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏱᎦᏬᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yi²³gạ³wo³nị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He may be speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The -i suffix which is used in imperatives is treated above as
        a variant of -a. An additional use of -i is shown in (110).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(110) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏱᏥᏬᏂᎯ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yị²jị²wo³ni²hi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"I can speak."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note that the expression of capability in (110) requires the y-
        prefix and the -i suffix. When another suffix intervenes, -i
        changes to -a, as in (111).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(111) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏱᏥᏬᏂᏏᎶᏣ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yị²jị²wo³ni²si²³lo³ja.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"I can speak over and over."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 293</p>
      <p><u>-vʔi, future imperative</u></p>
      <p>form: -vʔi.</p>
      <p>function: Future imperatives are formed by the use of -vʔi, as
        in (112b).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(112) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²³hi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hi²wo³ni²sv²ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak later."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>One or more suffixes may precede -vʔi in this construction, as
        in (113).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(113) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᏏᏙᎸᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo³ni²si²³do³²lv²ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Go around and speak later."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-gwu "only, just, still"</u></p>
      <p>form: -gwu.</p>
      <p>function: -gwu is used with the meaning "only" or "just" as in
        (115).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(114) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏊ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²hạ³gwu.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's just speaking." or "He's only speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When preceded by the adverb si, gwu means "still," as in (115).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(115) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">Ꮟ ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏊ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>si³ gạ²wo³nị²hạ³gwu.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's still speaking."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-sgo, interrogative</u></p>
      <p>form: -sgo.</p>
      <p>function: Questions which can be answered with yes or no are
        formed by the addition of -sgo, or by its short form -s, to verb
        forms; note (116) .</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(116) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is speaking."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏍᎪ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²ha³sgo?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he speaking?"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>c.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²has³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he speaking?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comments: -sgo must directly follow one of the prefixes shown
        at position 10 in Figure 1 above. It may be followed only by -hv
        "but." When -sgo is not followed by -hv, it ordinarily appears
        in its short form, -s, as in (116c).</p>
      <p><u>-ju, interrogative</u></p>
      <p>form: -ju.</p>
      <p>function: -ju is used with yes-no questions, but it carries an
        additional component of meaning not present in the case of -sgo;
        note (117).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(117) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏧ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²hạ³ju?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he speakingʔ"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>(117) would be an appropriate question to ask someone if a
        certain person who was expected to make a speech is speaking.
        Similarly, if the weather forecast called for snow, and someone
        goes to the window to see if snow is falling, a second person
        might ask the question in (118).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(118) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎫᏘᎭᏧ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gu²tị³hạ³ju?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Well, is it snowingʔ"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-ke "or"-interrogative</u></p>
      <p>form: -ke.</p>
      <p>function: -ke is attached to the second verb in disjunctive
        questions; see (119c).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(119) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᎣᏂᎭᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²has?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he speakingʔ"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td colspan="5">
              <hr color="darkgray">
              <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 294</p>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏕᎧᏃᎩᎠᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>de²³kạ³no²gi³ʔas³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he singingʔ"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>c.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏍ, ᏕᎧᏃᎩᎠᎨ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²has³, de²³kạ³no²gi³ʔạ³ke?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is he speaking or singing?</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-na "and what if?"</u></p>
      <p>form: -na.</p>
      <p>function: -na is an interrogative suffix which carries the
        meaning "and what if?" or "and what about?" Note (120).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(120) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏳᏬᏂᏌ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yụ³wo³ni²sa.</td>
            <td>"He may have spoken."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏳᏬᏂᏌᎾ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>yu²³wo³²ni⁴sạ²na¹?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"And what if he spokeʔ"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comments: -na is more frequently attached to nouns or pronouns,
        as in (121); see the discussion of nouns in <a
          href="#SectionII">Section II.</a></p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(121) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏂᎯᎾ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ni²hi⁴na¹?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"And what about you?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-hv "but"</u></p>
      <p>form : -hv.</p>
      <p>function: -hv occurs following -sgo to question an assertion,
        is appropriate as a reply to (122).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(122) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᏓᏛᏓᏍᏓ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e²da³²tv²da³²sda.</td>
            <td>"Let's you (pl) and I listen to him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(123)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎭᏍᎪᎲ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³nị²hạ³sgo¹hv?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"But is he speaking?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The question of (123) shows doubt that the man in (122) is
        really speaking. Note also (124), which could be asked as a
        response to a statement such as "Let's go see him."</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(124) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏝᏍᎪᎲ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo²³hlạ³sgo¹hv³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"But is he home?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-isi "or else"</u></p>
      <p>form: -isi.</p>
      <p>function: -isi is used with the meaning "or else," as in (125).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(125) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏣᎦᏎᏍᏕᏍᏗ, ᏘᏅᏥᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>jạ²ksẹ²sde³sdi, tị²nv³²ji³²si.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Be careful, or else you'll fall."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>comment: -isi always occurs in final position; it may be
        preceded by non-final suffixes, as in (126).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(126) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏙᏓᏣᎾᏒᏟᏙᎵᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>do²dạ³chạ³na³²sv²hli²³do³²li³²si.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Or else you're going to slide around."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>-dina, concessive imperative</u></p>
      <p>form: -dina.</p>
      <p>function: -dina may follow the imperative suffix to show that
        the speaker is willing for the person spoken to to perform the
        action expressed by the verb; note (127).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(127) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²³hi.</td>
            <td>"Speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᏬᏂᎯᏗᎾ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hị²wo¹ni²³hị³di³na.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Speak, then."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Forms such as (127b) imply that the speaker has been influenced
        to utter the imperative form by some consideration which has
        been brought to his attention.</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 295</p>
      <p><u>-dv,focus suffix</u></p>
      <p>form: -dv.</p>
      <p>function: -dv is used to indicate a kind of focus which is not
        fully understood. It frequently appears on verb forms used in
        replying to questions; note (129).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(128) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎫᏘᎭᏍ ᎠᎦᏍᎦᎨ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gu²tị³has³ a¹ga²sgạ³ke? </td>
            <td>"Is it snowing or raining?" </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(129) </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎦᏍᎦᏛ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹ga²sgạ³dv³. </td>
            <td>"It's raining." </td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>Notes on the co-occurrence of suffixes</u></p>
      <p>Several of the suffixes listed at position 10 on the chart in
        Figure 1 optionally drop the vowel -i when followed by -sgo,
        -ju, and -ke. These suffixes which drop -i are -vʔi, past; -eʔi,
        reportative; -oʔi, pluperfect; -oʔi, habitual. Note, for
        example, (130).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(130) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏎᎢᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo²ni²se³ʔis³?</td>
            <td>"Did he speak?"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏎᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²ses³?</td>
            <td>"Did he speak?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>A list of forms of the verb "to speak" containing two or
          more suffixes.</u> The forms contained in the following list
        illustrate the occurrence of two or more suffixes in a single
        verb form. It should be borne in mind that the total number of
        suffix combinations which is possible in Cherokee is actually
        much larger than the number of combinations found in the list,
        which is intended to be illustrative of the kind of complex verb
        forms which can occur.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏏᏏᏗ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³si⁴di.</td>
            <td>"He's about to make the same speech again."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏬᏂᏏᏏᏗᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wo³ni²si²³si³di¹sv²³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He was about to make the same speech again."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏏᎶᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si²³si³lọ²ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He will make the same speech repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎦᏬᏂᏏᏏᎶᎢᏏ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>dạ²gạ²wo³²ni²si²³si³lọ²ʔi³²si.</td>
            <td>"Or else he'll make the same speech repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎯᏍᏔᏃᎲᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²hị²stạ²nọ³hṿ³sga.</td>
            <td>"He's finishing using it to speak with."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏄᏬᏂᏏᏗᏎᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>nu²³wo³²ni²si²³di³²se⁴ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He had already been about to speak."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎶᏍᏗᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³lo³²sdị²ha.</td>
            <td>"He's using it to speak with repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎶᎥᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si³lọʔṿ²sga.</td>
            <td>"He's finishing speaking repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᎶᎡᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³lọ³ʔe¹ga.</td>
            <td>"He's going there to speak repeatedly."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᎯᏎᎴᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²hị²se²³le³²ga.</td>
            <td>"He's going there to speak for him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>

            <td>"He habitually goes around speaking."</td>

            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³lọ³ʔi²hị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He is coming to speak repeatedly."</td>

            <td>"He's going there to make the same speech repeatedly."</td>
