            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏏᎶᎡᎴᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³si³lọ²ʔe²le³ga.</td>
            <td>"He's going there to make the same speech repeatedly for
              him."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏬᏂᏏᏏᎶᎡᎴᎦᏍᎪᎲ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²wo³ni²si²³si³lọ²ʔe²le³gạ³sgo¹hv³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"But is he going there to make the same speech for him
              repeatedly?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>I-E.<a name="I-E"></a> <u>The reflexive, the passive, and
          classificatory verbs</u></p>
      <p><u>The reflexive.</u> There is a reflexive prefix in Cherokee
        which directly</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 296</p>
      <p>follows the pronoun prefix and precedes the verb stem. It
        appears as -adad- before a stem beginning with a vowel other
        than -a-, as -ad- before -a-, and as ada- before a stem
        beginning with a consonant; cf. (1-3).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(1) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎬᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gv²hnị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's hitting it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²dv²hnị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's hitting himself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(2)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏢᎢᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²hlv³ʔị²ha.</td>
            <td>"He's tying it up."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏢᎢᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²hlv³ʔi²ha.</td>
            <td>"He's tying himself up."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(3)</td>
            <td>a.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gowh²tị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He sees it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²gowh²tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He sees himself."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>When preceded by the Set B third person pronoun prefix u-, the
        initial -a- of -adad- is dropped; cf. (4a-b).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(4) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏩᏂᎸᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹wa²hnị³lv³ʔi.</td>
            <td>"He hit it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏓᏛᏂᎸᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹da²dv²hnị³lv³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He hit himself."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Note the following reflexive paradigms.</p>
      <p><u>Paradigm One: "to see oneself"</u></p>

        the stem of "to see," which begins with a consonant.</p>

      <p><u>Paradigm Three: "to hit oneself"</u></p>
      <p>This paradigm illustrates the use of the reflexive prefix,
        appearing as -adad-, before a verb stem beginning with a vowel
        other than -a-; as noted above, the reflexive appears as -ad-
        before a stem beginning with -a-.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>

            </td>
            <td>"I am hitting myself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎭᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>

            </td>
            <td>"You are hitting yourself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²dv²hnị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's hitting himself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᎾᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹nạ²da²dv²hnị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You and I are hitting ourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᏓᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>

      <p><u>Paradigm Five: "to forget oneself"</u></p>
      <p>"Forget" is a verb which ordinarily requires the Set B prefixes
        in all tenses. When the reflexive prefix is employed, however,
        verbs like "forget" follow the same pattern as those verbs which
        take Set A prefixes in the present tense (see Section <a
          href="#I-B">I-B</a> for discussion and illustrative
        paradigms). Note the use of the Set A prefixes in this paradigm,
        and the use of the Set B prefixes in Paradigm Six, in which
        reflexive forms of "forget" are shown in the non-progressive
        past. The</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 298</p>
      <p>pattern followed is thus like that of verbs like "hit" and "tie
        up," which take Set A prefixes in most tenses, but which require
        Set B prefixes in the non-progressive past (see Section <a
          href="#I-B">I-B</a> for paradigms of these verbs).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gạ²da²dv¹kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"I am forgetting myself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎭᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You are forgetting yourself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He is forgetting himself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᎾᏗᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹nạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You and I are forgetting ourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᏓᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹dạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) and I are forgetting ourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏍᏓᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>sdạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (dl) are forgetting youselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᏣᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹jạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) are forgetting yourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎾᏓᏛᎨᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹nạ²da²dv²kew²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They are forgetting themselves."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p><u>Paradigm Six: "to forget oneself," past tense</u></p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏆᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gwạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"I forgot myself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏣᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>jạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You forgot yourself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He forgot himself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎩᎾᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gị²nạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You and I forgot ourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᎦᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹gạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) and I forgot ourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏍᏓᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>sdạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (dl) forgot yourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎢᏣᏓᏛᎨᏫᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>i¹jạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) forgot yourselves."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎾᏓᏛᎨᏒᎢ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹nạ²da²dv²kew²sv²³ʔi.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They forgot themselves."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p> <u>The reciprocal.</u> Reciprocal forms, translated by "each
        other" in English, are formed in Cherokee by the use of the
        plural prefix de- together with -adad-, as in (5). (Note that
        de- appears as d- before a following vowel; see the discussion
        of de- in Section <a href="#I-A">I-A</a>.)</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(5) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎾᏓᏛᏂᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>da¹nạ²da²dv²hnị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They are hitting each other."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Verb forms combining de- and -adad- can also have a plural
        reflexive meaning. (5), for example, can also mean "they are
        hitting themselves," with the understanding that there are
        plural reflexive actions involved; i.e., each of the individuals
        involved is understood to be hitting himself separately. Note
        (6), in which it is understood either that the parties involved
        are tying each other up, or that each of the individuals in
        question are tying themselves separately.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(6) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏓᎾᏓᏢᎢᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>da²nạ²da²hlv³ʔị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They are tying each other up," "They are tying
              themselves up." (plural acts of tying)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>See (7), in which it is understood that the individuals
        referred to are tying themselves collectively.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(7) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎾᏓᏢᎢᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹nạ²da²hlv³ʔị²ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They are tying themselves." (a single act of tying)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The reciprocal meaning is impossible in the case of (7), since
        the absence of the prefix de- means that only a single act of
        tying is taking place.</p>
      <p><u>Other uses of the reflexive.</u>There is a non-reflexive use
        of -adad- which is possible only when there is no overtly
        expressed direct object; compare (8) and (9).</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 299</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(8) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎦᏯ ᎠᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²sgạ²ya a¹gowh²tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He sees a man."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(9)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²gowh²tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He sees (him)."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Form (10) is understood to mean "the man sees," not "he sees a
        man."</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(10)</td>
            <td><font color="red">*ạ²sgạ²ya a¹da²gowh²tị³ha.</font></td>
            <td>"He sees a man."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>This non-reflexive use of -adad- is possible only when it is
        understood that there is a covert animate direct object of the
        verb. In sentences in which an inanimate direct object is not
        overtly expressed, but is understood, forms without -adad- must
        be used, as in (11). It is important to note, however, that
        forms without -adad- can also be used when an animate direct
        object is understood.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(11) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gowh²ti³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He sees him, it."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>In situations in which an animate direct object is understood,
        but not overtly expressed, it is thus possible to find verb
        forms with or without -adad-. There are some restrictions,
        however; forms with -adad- may not be used with the habitual
        suffix, apparently. Note that (12) may be used as a response to
        a statement like "Tom works at Muskogee now," while (13), an
        ungrammatical form, cannot.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(12) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎯᎪᏩᏘᏍᎪᎢᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>hi²gowh¹ti²³sgo³ʔis³?</td>
            <td>"Do you (habitually) see him?"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(13)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><span style="color: red;">*****</span><br>
            </td>
            <td><font color="red">*hạ²da²gowh²ti²³sgọ³ʔis³?</font></td>
            <td>"Do you (habitually) see him?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>There are situations in which -adad- must be used when the
        animate direct object is not expressed overtly. Note (15), the
        response to (14).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(14) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">Ali ᎤᏍᏉᏟ ᎬᏂᎦ Foreman.&nbsp;
              <br>
            </td>
            <td>Ali u²sgwo²hli gvnh²ga Foreman. <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Foreman just hit Ali in the stomach." (immediate past)</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(15)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">AliᏛ ᎥᎠᏓᏛᏂᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>Alihnv ṿ²ʔạ²da²dvnh²ga.</td>
            <td>"And Ali just hit back."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>-adad- is apparently required with v- "back," in cases like
        (15). (Note that v- is a variant of i-, "again"; see Section <a
          href="#I-A">I-A</a>.)</p>
      <p>Non-reflexive -adad- must also be used with agentive forms,
        derived from verbs, when no direct object is specified; note
        (16-18).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(16) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᎯᎯ&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²da²³hị²hi</td>
            <td>"killer" (inanimate)</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(17)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᏗᏓᎯᎯ&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>di²da²³hị²hi</td>
            <td>"killer" (animate)</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(18)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎩᏓ ᏗᎯᎯ&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>gi²hli di²³hị²hi</td>
            <td>"dog killer" (animate or inanimate)</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Agentive forms never take -adad- when the direct object is
        specified, as in (18). An animate agentive with unspecified
        direct object must take -adad- preceded by the plural object
        prefix de-, as in (17). (Note the following changes which take
        place in the case of (17): de- becomes di-, a change which takes
        place in nouns; the initial -a- of -adad- deletes after -i-, and
        the final -d- of -adad- does not appear because the stem of
        "kill" begins with a consonant.) Note that the plural object
        prefix does not occur in the case of inanimate agentives with
        unspecified direct object, as in (16).</p>
      <p>It should also be pointed out that a question like (19) seems
        to carry a meaning component not present in forms such as (20).
        In (19), the question seems to imply that the person spoken of
        has at first not seen the person or persons, while in (20) there
        is no implication of this sort. In other words, (19) might be
        translated "is he beginning to see him" or "is he becoming aware
        of him by seeing him."</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(19) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏓᎪᏩᏘᎭᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹da²gowh²tị³has³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Does he see (him)?"</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td colspan="4">
              <hr color="darkgray">
              <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 300</p>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(20)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎪᏩᏘᎭᏍ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gowh²tị³has³?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Does he see him?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Verb forms which take the non-reflexive -adad- do not admit the
        plural object prefix de-; (19) could thus also mean "does he see
        (them)?" (20), on the other hand, can only mean "Does he see
        him, it?" Agentive forms like (17 -1 8) are exceptions.</p>
      <p>The non-reflexive use of the prefix -adad- is a fundamental
        aspect of Cherokee structure which requires further study.</p>
      <p><u>The Cherokee passive constructions</u></p>
      <p><u>The passive with unspecified actor.</u> There is a passive
        construction in Cherokee which is used when the agent performing
        the action of the verb is unspecified. This construction is
        illustrated in (21).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(21) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎦᏯ ᎠᏥᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²sgạ²ya a¹jị²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"A man is being seen."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>In (21) it is understood that a man is being seen by one or
        more unspecified individuals. Paradigms Five and Six illustrate
        the form that the special passive pronoun prefixes required by
        this construction take before consonants and vowels,
        respectively.</p>
      <p><u>Paradigm Five: "to be seen"</u></p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎥᎩᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>v¹gị²gowh²tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"I am being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᏣᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e¹jạ²gowh²tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏥᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹jị²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᎩᏂᏆᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e¹gị²ni¹gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You and I are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᎩᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e¹gi²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) and I are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᏍᏗᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e¹sdi²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (dl) are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎡᏥᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>e¹ji²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"You (pl) are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎨᏥᎪᏩᏘᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ge²jị²gowh¹tị³ha.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"They are being seen."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>

      <p><u>A second passive construction.</u> Cherokee exhibits a
        second passive construction which is formed by replacing the Set
        A pronoun prefix with the corresponding Set B prefix and
        inverting the order of the subject and direct object. Compare
        the passive sentence in (23) with the corresponding active
        sentence in (22).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">(22) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎨᏯ<br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎪᏩᏘᎭ<br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎦᏯ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">"A man sees a woman."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>&nbsp;<br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²ge²³hya</td>
            <td>a¹gowh²tị³ha</td>
            <td>ạ²sgạ²ya.</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>woman</td>
            <td>sees</td>
            <td>man</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;"><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">(23) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎦᏯ<br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎪᏩᏘᎭ<br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎨᏯ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">"A woman is being seen by a
              man."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²sgạ²ya</td>
            <td>u¹gowh²tị³ha</td>
            <td>ạ¹ge²³hya.</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>man</td>
            <td>is being seen</td>
            <td>woman</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The kind of passive illustrated by (23) can only be formed when
        both the subject and object of the verb are third person and
        when the verb is one which takes the Set A prefixes.
        Furthermore, even when these conditions are met, passives like
        (23) can only be formed in those tenses which allow the Set A
        prefixes. It would thus be impossible to form a passive from
        sentence (24), the past tense equivalent of (22). Passives like
        (23) can be formed in the immediate past tense, however, since
        the immediate past suffix takes Set A prefixes.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">(24) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎨᏯ <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎪᏩᏘᎭ <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎦᏯ. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">"A man saw a woman." <br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>&nbsp;<br>
            </td>
            <td>ạ²ge²³hya</td>
            <td>u¹gowh²tv²hv²³ʔi</td>
            <td>ạ²sgạ²ya.</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>woman</td>
            <td>saw</td>
            <td>man</td>
            <td><br>
            </td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The second passive requires that the recipient of the action be
        animate. The doer of the action may be either animate or
        inanimate; compare (25-26).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(25) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎦᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹ga²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"It's raining ."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(26)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎤᎦᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>u¹ga²sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"It's raining on him."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>Since the second passive construction can only be formed when
        both the subject and object are third person, there are only
        four possibilities for passivization: forms with third person
        singular subject and object (27), with third person singular
        subject and third person plural object (28), with third person
        plural subject and singular object (29), and with third person
        plural subject and object (30).</p>

      <p><u>A third passive construction.</u> There is a third
        construction in Cherokee which is sometimes best translated with
        English passive forms. This construction is marked by -ad-
        before vowels, by al- before -s-, -t-, and -k-, by ad- before
        vowels, by al- before the voiceless consonants -s-, -t-, and
        -k-, and by ali- before voiced consonants; cf. (35-37). It
        occurs only in the third person singular and seems to be used
        when the action expressed by the verb takes place without a
        human agent or when the action itself is being focused on as if
        there were no human agent.</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(35) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎪᏪᎵᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>go²hwe²³lị³ʔa.</td>
            <td>"He's writing it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏩᏙᏪᎵᎠ. <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹do²hwe²³li³ʔa.</td>
            <td>"It's being written."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(36) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏍᎪᎸᏗᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹sgo²³lv³dị²ʔa.</td>
            <td>"He's erasing it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎵᏍᎪᎸᏗᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>al¹sgo²³lv³dị²ʔa.</td>
            <td>"It's erasing itself."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(37) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎬᎭᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹gv²hạ²lị³ha.</td>
            <td>"He's cutting it out."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎵᎬᎭᎵᎭ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹lị²gv²hạ²lị³ha.</td>
            <td>"It's cutting itself out."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>(35b) would be appropriate in a situation in which a pen were
        seen writing by itself, without any apparent causality, and
        could be translated as "it's writing itself" instead of "it's
        being written." (36b) might be used to refer to a neon sign
        which goes off automatically. For a further instance of the
        third passive construction; note (38).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(38) <br>
            </td>
            <td>a. <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏑᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹su²³hwị³sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's painting it."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td><br>
            </td>
            <td>b.</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᎵᏑᏫᏍᎦ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>al¹su²³hwị³sga.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"It's being painted." or "It's painting itself."</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>The form in (38b) could be used in the sentence shown in (39).</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(39) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎣᏍᏗᏍ ᎠᎵᏑᏫᏍᎦ?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>o⁴sdas al¹su²³hwị³sga?&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"Is the painting going well?"</td>
          </tr>
        </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>In (39), although the painting is being carried out by an
        animate agent, the third passive is still used since the act of
        painting is focused on without regard for the person doing the
        painting. This construction requires further study and might
        more appropriately be termed a reflexive rather than a passive.</p>
      <p><u>Classificatory verbs.</u> There are a number of verbs in
        Cherokee which appear in one of several stem forms, depending on
        the nature of the direct object in the case of transitive verbs
        and on the nature of the subject in the case of intransitive
        verbs. These verbs are termed classificatory verbs; note, for
        example, (40-44).</p>
      <hr color="darkgray">
      <p style="color: rgb(128, 128, 128);">Page 303</p>
      <table>
        <tbody>
          <tr>
            <td>(40) <br>
            </td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᎧᎯᏯᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>ga²kạ²hi²yạ³ʔa.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"He's leaving a living thing behind."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(41)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎦᏁᎯᏯᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>

            </td>
            <td>"He's leaving a container of liquid behind."</td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
            <td>(42)</td>
            <td style="vertical-align: top;">ᎠᏗᏏᏯᎠ.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>a¹di³²si²yạ³ʔa.&nbsp; <br>
            </td>
            <td>"he's leaving a long object behind."</td>
